<p><b>Gap</b> (<small>French: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[ɡap]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>: <span lang="oc" xml:lang="oc"><i>Gap</i></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">commune</a> in southeastern France, the capital and largest town of the <a href="/wiki/Hautes-Alpes" title="Hautes-Alpes">Hautes-Alpes</a> <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">department</a>. At 750 m above sea level, it is France's highest <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_in_France" title="Prefectures in France">prefecture</a> (departmental capital).</p>
<p>Together with other Alpine towns, Gap engages in the <a href="/wiki/Alpine_Town_of_the_Year" title="Alpine Town of the Year">Alpine Town of the Year</a> Association for the implementation of the <a href="/wiki/Alpine_Convention" title="Alpine Convention">Alpine Convention</a> to achieve sustainable development in the Alpine Arc.</p>
<p>Gap was awarded <a href="/wiki/Alpine_Town_of_the_Year" title="Alpine Town of the Year">Alpine Town of the Year</a> in 2002. In 2013 Gap was named the sportiest city in France by the national sports newspaper <a href="/wiki/L%27%C3%89quipe" title="L'Équipe">L'Équipe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:652px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gap_Pan01.jpg"><img alt="A panoramic view of Gap" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="8872" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Gap_Pan01.jpg/650px-Gap_Pan01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Gap_Pan01.jpg/975px-Gap_Pan01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Gap_Pan01.jpg/1300px-Gap_Pan01.jpg 2x" width="650"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gap_Pan01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A panoramic view of Gap</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alpine</a> crossroads at the intersection of D994 and the Route nationale 85, or <a href="/wiki/Route_Napol%C3%A9on" title="Route Napoléon">Route Napoléon</a>, which crosses the <a href="/wiki/Col_Bayard" title="Col Bayard">Col Bayard</a> north of the city, Gap is located between the historic <a href="/wiki/Dauphin%C3%A9" title="Dauphiné">Dauphiné</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" title="Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur">Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur</a> administrative region. With its 40,761 inhabitants (2012), it is the main town of an urban area of 62,072 inhabitants (2011),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> which is the main town of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alpes_du_Sud_(France)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alpes du Sud (France) (page does not exist)">Alpes du Sud</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpes_du_Sud_(France)" title="fr:Alpes du Sud (France)">fr</a>)</span>. 745 metres (2,400 ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>, at the right bank of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luye_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luye River (page does not exist)">Luye River</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luye" title="fr:Luye">fr</a>)</span>, close to where it joins the <a href="/wiki/Durance" title="Durance">Durance River</a> to the north, Gap is in the midst of a rich and preserved natural environment, south-west of the <a href="/wiki/%C3%89crins_National_Park" title="Écrins National Park">Écrins National Park</a>, south-east of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Massif_du_D%C3%A9voluy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Massif du Dévoluy (page does not exist)">Dévoluy massif</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massif_du_D%C3%A9voluy" title="fr:Massif du Dévoluy">fr</a>)</span> and west of the <a href="/wiki/Lac_de_Serre-Pon%C3%A7on" title="Lac de Serre-Ponçon">Lac de Serre-Ponçon</a>. The region around Gap is known as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gapen%C3%A7ais&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gapençais (page does not exist)">Gapençais</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gapen%C3%A7ais" title="fr:Gapençais">fr</a>)</span>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology_and_terrain">Geology and terrain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geology and terrain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The commune of Gap is almost entirely located in the <i>Sillon de Gap</i> [Gap trench],<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> a wide valley bottom located about 735 metres (2,411 ft) above sea level and including the western slopes almost 2,000 metres (6,600 ft) (Charance mountain and pic de Gleize).</p>
<p>The highest point of the municipality is however outside this great valley, on another watershed slope, the Raz de Bec, at 2,385 metres (7,825 ft), is within the limits of the commune, and was in the former commune of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chaudun_(Hautes-Alpes)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chaudun (Hautes-Alpes) (page does not exist)">Chaudun</a>, which merged with Gap in the 19th century.</p>
<p>This valley was shaped by the <i>Glacier de la Durance</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> during the last ice age, known as the <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">Würm glaciation</a>.</p>
<p>Thus, soils are very often formed by <a href="/wiki/Moraine" title="Moraine">moraine</a> deposits. No less than five levels of lateral and frontal moraines are observable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> These are clearly visible, especially on the southern slopes of the Col Bayard, where they were formed in places of the terraces used by agriculture.</p>
<p>In retreating, the glacier also left <a href="/wiki/Glacial_erratic" title="Glacial erratic">erratics</a> of several metres high. Examples include, among others, the erratic boulders of <i>Peyre-Ossel</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> and <i>Justice</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The glacier, which in the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">Quaternary</a> has shaped the <i>Sillon de Gap</i>, presented several <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Diffluence_(glaciology)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Diffluence (glaciology) (page does not exist)">diffluences</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diffluence_(glaciologie)" title="fr:Diffluence (glaciologie)">fr</a>)</span>: one to the glacier of the <a href="/wiki/Drac_(river)" title="Drac (river)">Drac</a> from the cols of <a href="/wiki/Col_de_Manse" title="Col de Manse">Manse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Col_Bayard" title="Col Bayard">Bayard</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> and one towards the <a href="/wiki/Bu%C3%ABch" title="Buëch">Buëch</a> Valley by the <a href="/wiki/La_Freissinouse" title="La Freissinouse">La Freissinouse</a> border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The cover of morainic debris is omnipresent in the <i>Sillon de Gap</i> but is not the only vestige of the Quaternary glaciation. There is also the typical topography of glacial valleys. The location of the town of Gap corresponds to an <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ombilic_glaciaire&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ombilic glaciaire (page does not exist)"><i>Ombilic glaciaire</i></a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ombilic_glaciaire" title="fr:Ombilic glaciaire">fr</a>)</span>, where large quantities of clay were deposited. Upstream lies the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Verrou_glaciaire&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Verrou glaciaire (page does not exist)">Verrou glaciaire</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Verrou_glaciaire" title="fr:Verrou glaciaire">fr</a>)</span> [glacial lock] of Pont-Sarrazin and downstream of Tourronde.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The mechanical action of the <i>glacier de la Durance</i> was facilitated by the presence of relatively friable layers. The part which is central and south-east of the town consists mainly of soft rocks (<a href="/wiki/Callovian" title="Callovian">Callovo</a>-<a href="/wiki/Oxfordian_(stage)" title="Oxfordian (stage)">Oxfordian</a> black <a href="/wiki/Marl" title="Marl">marl</a>). They consist of soft <a href="/wiki/Schist" title="Schist">schist</a> of bluish or brown colors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> In the northwestern part are the harder rocks of lighter colours, <a href="/wiki/Tithonian" title="Tithonian">Tithonian</a> <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, formed in places of rocky bars or cornices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerycaption">The geology and terrain of Gap</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrography">Hydrography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Hydrography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The town of Gap is crossed by the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luye_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luye River (page does not exist)">Luye River</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luye" title="fr:Luye">fr</a>)</span>, a tributary of the <a href="/wiki/Durance" title="Durance">Durance</a> which has a total course of 22.6 kilometres (14.0 mi). During its passage through the commune, the Luye receives several torrents. It merges on the right bank with the 5.1 kilometres (3.2 mi) long <i>Buzon</i>, the <i>Bonne</i> (9.4 kilometres (5.8 mi)) and the <i>torrent du Cristaye</i> (2.4 kilometres (1.5 mi)); and on the left bank, the <i>La Magdeleine Canal</i> (5.3 kilometres (3.3 mi)), the <i>Riotord</i> (4.8 kilometres (3.0 mi)) and the <i>torrent du Partiment</i>, (6.7 kilometres (4.2 mi)) long.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Even if the Luye hydrographic basin represents the largest share of the commune, waters at the southwest of the commune (the Saint-Jean quarter) drain into the torrent of Malecombe, a tributary of the Rousine, which flows into the Durance south of Tallard.</p>
<p>In the northwest of the commune (located on the other side of the col de Gleize) lie the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Petit_Bu%C3%ABch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Petit Buëch (page does not exist)">Petit Buëch</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petit_Bu%C3%ABch" title="fr:Petit Buëch">fr</a>)</span> sources. Around 1,700 metres (5,600 ft) above sea level, they are formed by several streams which converge at the old village of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chaudun_(Hautes-Alpes)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chaudun (Hautes-Alpes) (page does not exist)">Chaudun</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaudun_(Hautes-Alpes)" title="fr:Chaudun (Hautes-Alpes)">fr</a>)</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Accueil_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Accueil-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Finally, an important channel feeds Gap with <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">drinking water</a> and water for <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a>: The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Canal_de_Gap&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Canal de Gap (page does not exist)"><i>Canal de Gap</i></a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canal_de_Gap" title="fr:Canal de Gap">fr</a>)</span>, or <i>Canal du Drac</i>, about 30 kilometres (19 mi) long, leads the water captured in the <a href="/wiki/Drac_(river)" title="Drac (river)">Drac</a> via a tunnel under the <a href="/wiki/Col_de_Manse" title="Col de Manse">Col de Manse</a> to the Jaussauds reservoir (altitude 1,141 metres (3,743 ft))<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Accueil_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Accueil-15">[15]</a></sup> where it divides into two branches, including the main branch which bypasses Gap west to Correo through Charance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Its temperate climate is influenced by a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (hot and dry summers) and also an <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">Alpine climate</a> (cold winters).</p>
<p>Thus the main feature of the local climate is the importance of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insolation" title="Insolation">sunshine</a> enjoyed by the city. Furthermore, <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">snowfall</a> underscores the mountain character of the city. <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">Thunderstorms</a> are frequent in summer, <a href="/wiki/Fog" title="Fog">fog</a> is rather rare.</p>

<p>Comparisons with surveys of the period 1878-1940 showed lower maximum averages over the period 1950-1970 for the winter and summer months. Over the same period, again for the winter and summer months, there was an increase in the average minimum. Thus the evolution of the climate tends towards a slight reduction of differences in winter temperatures on the one hand, and summer on the other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refClim2Gap_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-refClim2Gap-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Extreme temperatures also highlight the mountain and Mediterranean components of the climate. Indeed, over the decade 1951-1960 the absolute minimum recorded was −18 °C (−0.4 °F) on 3 February 1956. While the absolute maximum was of 36.5 °C (97.7 °F) observed July 8, 1952.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refClim2Gap_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-refClim2Gap-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Below is the average monthly rainfall.</p>

<div class="thumbcaption">

The "bar Bayard", synonymous with good weather over the city</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Outside of the valley breezes, the prevailing wind is from the north, locally named the <i>bise</i> wind. In fact, it is a component of the <a href="/wiki/Mistral_(wind)" title="Mistral (wind)">mistral</a>. Up the <a href="/wiki/Drac_(river)" title="Drac (river)">Drac</a> Valley, this wind crosses the Bayard plateau down to Gap. When it carries clouds, there is the phenomenon of "the bar of Bayard": a compact pile of clouds covering the Bayard plateau. Pushed by the wind, they descend into the valley. Under the effect of the increase in pressure and temperature, these clouds disappear immediately a few hundred metres further down. Even in perpetual motion, cloud cover appears motionless. If these conditions are synonymous with freshness in autumn and spring, and bright cold in the winter, they are always accompanied by a perfectly sunny and clear atmosphere above the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-refClim2Gap_20-4"><a href="#cite_note-refClim2Gap-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Channels_of_communication_and_transport">Channels of communication and transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Channels of communication and transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GapCarto01.svg"><img alt="Map of transport in Gap" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1500" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/GapCarto01.svg/220px-GapCarto01.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/GapCarto01.svg/330px-GapCarto01.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/GapCarto01.svg/440px-GapCarto01.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GapCarto01.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of transport in Gap</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_network">Road network</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Road network">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The town of Gap lies at a crossroads. The route nationale <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Route_nationale_85_(France)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Route nationale 85 (France) (page does not exist)">RN 85</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Route_nationale_85_(France)" title="fr:Route nationale 85 (France)">fr</a>)</span> heads towards the north and the south, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Route_nationale_94_(France)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Route nationale 94 (France) (page does not exist)">RN 94</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Route_nationale_94_(France)" title="fr:Route nationale 94 (France)">fr</a>)</span> to the east and the departmental RD 994 road to the west.</p>
<p>The RN 85 travels 103 kilometres (64 mi) north to <a href="/wiki/Grenoble" title="Grenoble">Grenoble</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sisteron" title="Sisteron">Sisteron</a> is located 48 kilometres (30 mi) in the opposite direction, and eventually also to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a>. The RN 94 travels 87 kilometres (54 mi) to reach <a href="/wiki/Brian%C3%A7on" title="Briançon">Briançon</a> and towards <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Col_de_Montgen%C3%A8vre" title="Col de Montgenèvre">Col de Montgenèvre</a>. Meanwhile, the RD 994 joins with <a href="/wiki/Pont-Saint-Esprit" title="Pont-Saint-Esprit">Pont-Saint-Esprit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gard" title="Gard">Gard</a>, more than 150 kilometres (93 mi) distant.</p>
<p>15 km (9 mi) separates Gap from <a href="/wiki/La_Saulce" title="La Saulce">La Saulce</a> on the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Autoroute_A51_(France)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Autoroute A51 (France) (page does not exist)">A51</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autoroute_A51_(France)" title="fr:Autoroute A51 (France)">fr</a>)</span> motorway. This highway provides fast travel to <a href="/wiki/Aix-en-Provence" title="Aix-en-Provence">Aix-en-Provence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a> 170 kilometres (110 mi) away, via the <a href="/wiki/Durance" title="Durance">Durance</a> Valley. A planned extension of this highway to the north, to the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Col_du_Fau&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Col du Fau (page does not exist)">Col du Fau</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Col_du_Fau" title="fr:Col du Fau">fr</a>)</span> seems definitively buried. Although it has been desired by elected officials for the voters and the State, in order to divert trucks from the <a href="/wiki/A7_autoroute" title="A7 autoroute">A7</a>, the absence of this highway has not created the announced decline. On the contrary, the city ceased to grow (see demographics) without being absorbed by its relatively distant neighbours thanks precisely to its relative isolation from the main road network, including Grenoble (in no effect a dormitory community).</p>
<p>Taking into account the increase in road traffic, the creation of an urban boulevard became a prospect of improvement. This one 9 kilometres (5.6 mi) long and comprising several structures, could bypass the city from the west. Concerning also the transit of traffic serving the city itself, it would act as a <a href="/wiki/Bypass_(road)" title="Bypass (road)">bypass</a>, leaving the RN 85, close to the area of Micropolis to the southwest and lead to the RN 94, north-east towards the Romette intersection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: [[:<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gare_de_Gap&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gare de Gap (page does not exist)">Gare de Gap</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gare_de_Gap" title="fr:Gare de Gap">fr</a>)</span>]]</div>
<p>The city is served by <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a>.</p>
<p>Gap is connected directly to <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> daily by a sleeper train (the <a href="/wiki/Sleeping_car" title="Sleeping car">sleeping car</a> was removed in 2007) network <a href="/wiki/Intercit%C3%A9s" title="Intercités">Intercités</a> <i>at night</i>, but also by <a href="/wiki/Corail_(train)" title="Corail (train)">Corail</a> or <a href="/wiki/Transport_express_r%C3%A9gional" title="Transport express régional">TER</a> to <a href="/wiki/Brian%C3%A7on" title="Briançon">Briançon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenoble" title="Grenoble">Grenoble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valence,_Dr%C3%B4me" title="Valence, Drôme">Valence</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Valence-Ville" title="Gare de Valence-Ville">Gare de Valence-Ville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Valence_TGV" title="Gare de Valence TGV">Gare de Valence TGV</a>), as well as to <a href="/wiki/Aix-en-Provence" title="Aix-en-Provence">Aix-en-Provence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>.</p>
<p>In the 1930s, work aimed at the establishment of a metric line between Gap and Corps by the <a href="/wiki/Col_de_Manse" title="Col de Manse">Col de Manse</a> was undertaken. These were never finished and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Line_of_the_Champsaur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Line of the Champsaur (page does not exist)">line of the Champsaur</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ligne_du_Champsaur" title="fr:Ligne du Champsaur">fr</a>)</span> was never born. Portions were reused for the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Route_nationale" title="Route nationale">route nationale</a>.</p>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ligne_de_Chorges_%C3%A0_Barcelonnette&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ligne de Chorges à Barcelonnette (page does not exist)">line to Barcelonnette</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ligne_de_Chorges_%C3%A0_Barcelonnette" title="fr:Ligne de Chorges à Barcelonnette">fr</a>)</span> was also begun in the east, but never completed. A double curve viaduct remains beneath the waters of the Lac de Serre-Ponçon.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">Air transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Air transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Located 13 kilometres (8.1 mi) from Gap, the <a href="/wiki/Gap%E2%80%93Tallard_Airport" title="Gap–Tallard Airport">Gap–Tallard Airport</a> can handle passenger traffic.</p>
<p>The company <a href="/wiki/Air_Alpes" title="Air Alpes">Air Alpes</a> operated a <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Canada_DHC-6_Twin_Otter" title="De Havilland Canada DHC-6 Twin Otter">DHC-6 Twin otter</a>, with a regular service between <a href="/wiki/Paris%E2%80%93Le_Bourget_Airport" title="Paris–Le Bourget Airport">Paris-Le Bourget</a> and Gap from 1973 to 1977, since abandoned. The vast majority of air movements are sports-oriented.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_transport">Urban transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Urban transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Public transport in the city is provided by the Linea network. In 2016, the network is comprised 12 lines. There is also a school transport service, a shuttle between <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Domaine_de_Charance&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Domaine de Charance (page does not exist)">Domaine de Gap-Charance</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domaine_de_Charance" title="fr:Domaine de Charance">fr</a>)</span>/Centre-ville/Gap-Bayard runs in July and August, a shuttle to the hyper-Centre and a taxibus is available on demand. Aside from the taxibus, all of these are totally <a href="/wiki/Free_public_transport" title="Free public transport">free services</a> for users.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cycling_facilities">Cycling facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cycling facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Several cycle paths traverse the city. Some are separate from the road network, others are cycle lanes alongside roads.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanism">Urbanism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Urbanism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Of the 21,479 houses in Gap in 2011, 88% were principal residences (against 89.20% of 19,043 houses in 2006), and 8.50% were vacant (compared with 7% of the 19,043 in 2006). Two thirds of them are <a href="/wiki/Apartment" title="Apartment">apartments</a> (almost 65%). A majority of these houses consist of 4 rooms (30%) or 5 rooms (28%). Overall, the buildings date from the period between 1946-1990 (65%). Half of the inhabitants of principal residences are owners (51%), the share of social rental housing (<a href="/wiki/HLM" title="HLM">HLM</a>) represents only 15%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insee05061_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-insee05061-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Amenity_projects">Amenity projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Amenity projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>A ring road, now called <i>boulevard urbain</i> [urban boulevard]</li>
<li>The Bernard-Givaudan park and garden<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li>Renovation of the <i>Rue Jean Eymard</i> [Jean Eymard Road]<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li>Renovation of the <i>Carré de l'Imprimerie</i> [Printing House Square] in the town centre with a number of facilities (housing, commercial space, underground parking, medical home, etc.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gap006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Gap006.jpg/220px-Gap006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Gap006.jpg/330px-Gap006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Gap006.jpg/440px-Gap006.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gap006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bilingual_sign" title="Bilingual sign">Bilingual signage</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vivaro-Alpine_dialect" title="Vivaro-Alpine dialect">Alpine Provençal</a> and in <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> at Gap</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first attestation of the name of the city is located in the ancient texts as <i>Vappincum</i>, later reduced to <i>Vappum</i>, the form of Gap is found in the 13th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>The toponym <i>Vappincum</i> is analyzed on the basis of a radical <i>Vapp-</i> unknown meaning, and the suffix <i>-incu</i> of <a href="/wiki/Ligurian_(Romance_language)" title="Ligurian (Romance language)">Ligurian</a> origin found in Provence and the Massif central to the Alps (cf. <a href="/wiki/Arlanc" title="Arlanc">Arlanc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marnhagues-et-Latour" title="Marnhagues-et-Latour">Nonenque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moirans" title="Moirans">Moirans</a> and <i>Morencum</i> in the 10th century and Lemenc, a district of Chambéry, formerly <i>Lemencum</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The Gap form actually began as the short form <i>Vappum</i>, well attested, by the final drop.</p>
<p>The v- has been radically treated as a w- Germanic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> where <i>*Wap</i>, then Gap (see for this type of evolution the <a href="/wiki/Wasp" title="Wasp">wasp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>vespa</i>, treats words as <i>*wespa</i>; <a href="/wiki/Viscum_album" title="Viscum album">mistletoe</a>, Latin <i>viscum</i>, treated as <i>*wiscum</i>, etc.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[note 1]</a></sup> depending on the phonetic path [w] &gt; [gw] &gt; [g]). This phonetic evolution would be more specifically made under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_language" title="Gothic language">Gothic language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>The name in <a href="/wiki/Proven%C3%A7al_dialect" title="Provençal dialect">Provençal</a> (Alpine) is also <i>Gap</i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first settlement of Gap dates back to the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDLV4_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-HDLV4-32">[31]</a></sup> The culture of these first inhabitants belonged to the southern <a href="/wiki/Chass%C3%A9en_culture" title="Chasséen culture">Chasséen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Very rare testimonies of the pre-Roman era are formed by the remains of an <a href="/wiki/Oppidum" title="Oppidum">oppidum</a> located at the summit of the hill of <i>Saint-Mens</i> with few visible traces of a dolmen uncovered in 1866<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> and an ancient cemetery in the hamlet of Pré Camargue; but no remains were kept of these last two findings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> Gallic money was also found. Gap was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celto</a>-<a href="/wiki/Ligures" title="Ligures">Ligurian</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tricorii&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tricorii (page does not exist)">Tricorii</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tricorii" title="fr:Tricorii">fr</a>)</span> tribe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> These peoples, probably belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Caturiges" title="Caturiges">Caturiges</a> tribe, spoke the Celtic language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Roman_period">The Roman period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: The Roman period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RomanAlps.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="457" data-file-width="582" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/RomanAlps.jpg/220px-RomanAlps.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/RomanAlps.jpg/330px-RomanAlps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/RomanAlps.jpg/440px-RomanAlps.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RomanAlps.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Roman roads in the Alps, during the 4th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gapen%C3%A7ais&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gapençais (page does not exist)">Gapençais</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gapen%C3%A7ais" title="fr:Gapençais">fr</a>)</span> was then part of the territory of the <a href="/wiki/Vocontii" title="Vocontii">Vocontii</a>, a Gallic people who were Romanised during the conquest of <a href="/wiki/Gallia_Narbonensis" title="Gallia Narbonensis">Gallia Narbonensis</a> in 125-124 BC, whose capitals were <a href="/wiki/Luc-en-Diois" title="Luc-en-Diois">Luc-en-Diois</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vaison-la-Romaine" title="Vaison-la-Romaine">Vaison</a>.</p>
<p>Around 20 BC, <a href="/wiki/Cottius" title="Cottius">Cottius</a>, a leader of tribes of the Valley of <a href="/wiki/Suze,_Dr%C3%B4me" title="Suze, Drôme">Suze</a>, allied to Rome, and urged by <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a>, undertook the building of a route of communication in the Valley of the <a href="/wiki/Durance" title="Durance">Durance</a>. He had to submit the various peoples concerned, who were eager to maintain their independence. This route, built between 14 and 6 BC, and which received the name of <i>Via Cottia per Alpem</i>, linked <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a> to <a href="/wiki/Sisteron" title="Sisteron">Sisteron</a> and consisted of six stations. Then known as <i>Vapincum</i>, the town of Gap was founded from one of these stations. In 22 AD, Gap became the start of a Roman road to <a href="/wiki/Valence,_Dr%C3%B4me" title="Valence, Drôme">Valence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDLV7-9_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-HDLV7-9-38">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>At this time, the location of the future city was a Roman camp. The camp was protected by a terraced wall surrounded by a ditch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> It was the largest between <a href="/wiki/Montgen%C3%A8vre" title="Montgenèvre">Montgenèvre</a> and Sisteron. The garrison that occupied it could be estimated at 360 men. They came from the surrounding peoples. They were assigned to protect users of the Roman roads against looters. Later, an axis towards the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Champsaur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Champsaur (page does not exist)">Champsaur</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Champsaur" title="fr:Champsaur">fr</a>)</span> was created. The Gap site took importance by becoming a hub of communications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDLV7-9_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-HDLV7-9-38">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>The economy was mainly pastoral and the first crops grew on the slopes of <i>Puymaure</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDLV7-9_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-HDLV7-9-38">[37]</a></sup> Some houses were built on stilts as shown by excavations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDLV4_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-HDLV4-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the first centuries, the population increased significantly. Towards the end of the 3rd century and 4th century, a new fortification was built. These ramparts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> which completely surrounded the first enclosure, were composed of eleven ratings and eleven towers that protected the inhabitants of the city from barbarian invasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> With an enclosed area of 2 hectares (4.9 acres), Gap made a big village.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From 28 December 986, the Bishop of Gap had sovereignty over the city due to concerns about future Muslim invasions, and held that power until Revolutionary reforms in 1801 despite Gap being annexed by the French crown in 1512.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Gap and its area became part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/County_of_Provence" title="County of Provence">County of Provence</a>, established at the end of the 10th century, and then by the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Forcalquier" title="County of Forcalquier">County of Forcalquier</a>, which separated in the 12th century. The Bishops of Gap were also the temporal lords of the city. But their control was long disputed by officers of the Counts of Forcalquier, notably under the episcopate of Arnoux, who later became the bishop of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> On the death of the last Count of <a href="/wiki/County_of_Forcalquier" title="County of Forcalquier">Forcalquier</a> in 1209, the Embrun and Gap areas were passed to the <a href="/wiki/Dauphin%C3%A9" title="Dauphiné">Dauphiné</a> while those of Forcalquier and Sisteron returned to the County of Provence. It is for this reason that the current coat of arms of the Region Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur is the coat of arms of the Dauphiné. In 1349 the Dauphin of Viennois <a href="/wiki/Humbert_II_of_Viennois" title="Humbert II of Viennois">Humbert II</a> passed on his Principality to the eldest son of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippe_VI_of_France" title="Philippe VI of France">Philippe VI of France</a>, the future King of France <a href="/wiki/Charles_V_of_France" title="Charles V of France">Charles V</a>. From 1349 to 1457 Dauphiné remained a Principality separated from France, whose prince was the eldest son of the King of France. In 1457, <a href="/wiki/Charles_VII_of_France" title="Charles VII of France">Charles VII</a> put an end to this status and joined the province to the Kingdom of France.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Knights_Templar" title="Knights Templar">Knights Templar</a> owned a house at Gap, a secondary establishment which depended on a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Templar_commanderies_in_Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="List of Templar commanderies in Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur (page does not exist)">commandery</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liste_des_commanderies_templi%C3%A8res_en_Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" title="fr:Liste des commanderies templières en Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur">fr</a>)</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> The creation of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Consulat_(Ancien_R%C3%A9gime)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Consulat (Ancien Régime) (page does not exist)">Consulate</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consulat_(Ancien_R%C3%A9gime)" title="fr:Consulat (Ancien Régime)">fr</a>)</span>, which ruled the city, dated back to before 1209.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 14th century, the city took advantage of the benefits of the installation of the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Popes</a> in <a href="/wiki/Avignon" title="Avignon">Avignon</a>, which brought a more frequent passage of travellers to develop a <a href="/wiki/Handicraft" title="Handicraft">craft</a> of wool and skins, which made it thrive. Avignon linkages were strengthened by the presence of many clerics of the entourage of the Pope, within the chapter of the canons of Gap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renaissance_and_early_modern_era">Renaissance and early modern era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Renaissance and early modern era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gap030.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1448" data-file-width="2512" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Gap030.jpg/220px-Gap030.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Gap030.jpg/330px-Gap030.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Gap030.jpg/440px-Gap030.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gap030.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gap in 1607</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 16th and 17th centuries were particularly dark times for the city. The <a href="/wiki/French_Wars_of_Religion" title="French Wars of Religion">Wars of Religion</a> were lethal in the region. Gap was a <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> stronghold, while the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Champsaur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Champsaur (page does not exist)">Champsaur</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Champsaur" title="fr:Champsaur">fr</a>)</span> switched to <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>. After various skirmishes, <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Bonne,_Duke_of_Lesdigui%C3%A8res" title="François de Bonne, Duke of Lesdiguières">François de Bonne</a>, leader of the Protestants, decided to attack Gap, nevertheless protected by 20 towers. On the night of 3 January 1577, François Philibert, known as <i>Cadet de Charance</i>, opened the Saint-Arey gate, and allowed him to attack the city by surprise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-duchamblo126_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-duchamblo126-48">[47]</a></sup> To cries of "Kill! Kill!" his men proceeded in veritable butchery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> De Bonne burned the cathedral, plundered the monasteries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-duchamblo126_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-duchamblo126-48">[47]</a></sup> appropriated the property of the inhabitants, and built a proud citadel on the <i>Colline de Puymaur</i>e [Puymaure Hill] where it dominated over Gap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> Returned to Catholicism in 1622, he abandoned all claims to the city.</p>
<p>In 1692, the troops of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Piedmont&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="History of Piedmont (page does not exist)">Piedmontese</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Histoire_du_Pi%C3%A9mont" title="fr:Histoire du Piémont">fr</a>)</span> ruler <a href="/wiki/Victor_Amadeus_II_of_Sardinia" title="Victor Amadeus II of Sardinia">Victor Amadeus II</a>, committed with the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Alliance_(League_of_Augsburg)" title="Grand Alliance (League of Augsburg)">League of Augsburg</a>, against the France of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV</a>, captured the city, abandoned by its inhabitants, on 29 August. Gap was looted and burned,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> of the 953 houses in the commune, 798 were destroyed.</p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: [[:<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Invasion_of_Dauphine_in_1692&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Invasion of Dauphine in 1692 (page does not exist)">Invasion of Dauphine in 1692</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invasion_of_Dauphine_in_1692" title="fr:Invasion of Dauphine in 1692">fr</a>)</span>]]</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gap029.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="459" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Gap029.jpg/220px-Gap029.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Gap029.jpg/330px-Gap029.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Gap029.jpg/440px-Gap029.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gap029.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gap at the end of the 18th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1790, during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, the province of <a href="/wiki/Dauphin%C3%A9" title="Dauphiné">Dauphiné</a> was divided into three departments: <a href="/wiki/Dr%C3%B4me" title="Drôme">Drôme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Is%C3%A8re" title="Isère">Isère</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hautes-Alpes" title="Hautes-Alpes">Hautes-Alpes</a> which Gap became the <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_in_France" title="Prefectures in France">prefecture</a>. Hautes-Alpes then became the highest Department of France and Gap, the highest prefecture of the country. It remains prefecture of Haute-Alpes to this day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1802, the <a href="/wiki/Baron" title="Baron">baron</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Charles-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Ladoucette&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Charles-François de Ladoucette (page does not exist)">Charles-François de Ladoucette</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Ladoucette" title="fr:Charles-François de Ladoucette">fr</a>)</span> was appointed <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_prefects_of_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="List of prefects of Hautes-Alpes (page does not exist)">Prefect of the Hautes-Alpes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liste_des_pr%C3%A9fets_des_Hautes-Alpes" title="fr:Liste des préfets des Hautes-Alpes">fr</a>)</span>. Under his administration, the city of Gap and the Department of the Hautes-Alpes experienced some growth. It built roads linking Gap to Italy and the Drôme Valley and created a departmental nursery. His statue, carved by the Gap sculptor Jean Marcellin, was erected in 1866 at the square which bears his name.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gap031.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1266" data-file-width="2106" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Gap031.jpg/220px-Gap031.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Gap031.jpg/330px-Gap031.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Gap031.jpg/440px-Gap031.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gap031.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gap, the Lignole Gate in 1830</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" title="Napoleon I of France">Napoleon I</a> left <a href="/wiki/Elba" title="Elba">Elba</a> in February 1815 and stopped at Gap on 5 March 1815 with 40 horsemen and 10 grenadiers, where he had thousands of copies of his Proclamations printed. The whole population of the city accompanied Napoleon when he left Gap. Acknowledging the reception of the population of these regions, he left the Haut-Alpins with the following message:</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;"><i>The inhabitants of the departments of the high and low Alps, citizens,</i>
<p><i>I was deeply touched by all the feelings that you have shown me, your wishes are granted. The cause of the Nation will triumph again. You're right to call me your father; I live for the honour and happiness of France. My return banishes all your concerns; it ensures the conservation of all properties, equality among all classes and the rights you have enjoyed for the last 25 years, and after which our fathers have so yearned, forming today a part of your existence.</i></p>
<p><i>In all circumstances where I find myself, I will always remember with great interest all that I've seen through your country.</i></p>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VilleGap058.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1875" data-file-width="2500" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/VilleGap058.jpg/220px-VilleGap058.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/VilleGap058.jpg/330px-VilleGap058.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/VilleGap058.jpg/440px-VilleGap058.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VilleGap058.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fresco of the city center of Gap in 1899</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Gap experienced a new era from 1875 with the arrival of the railway.</p>
<p>The commune of <i>Chaudun</i> was joined with Gap, by the prefectoral Decree of 22 October 1895.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During World War II, the city was part of the free zone. But after November 1942 and the <a href="/wiki/Case_Anton" title="Case Anton">Case Anton</a>, it was integrated into the occupied area. After <a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">Operation Overlord</a> on 6 June 1944, the Germans placed some 1,000 men to hold the <i>cuvette de Gap</i> [Gap Basin], a key point of the Cannes-Lyon axis. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jean_Drouot-L%27Hermine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jean Drouot-L'Hermine (page does not exist)">Jean Drouot-L'Hermine</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Drouot-L%27Hermine" title="fr:Jean Drouot-L'Hermine">fr</a>)</span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> 37 years old, an original Gaullist resistant and accomplished soldier (he had trained more than 4000 resistance fighters in combat and about a hundred in sabotage) was sent by the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Government_of_the_French_Republic" title="Provisional Government of the French Republic">GPRF</a> of <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">General de Gaulle</a> to liberate the city on behalf of the Resistance. Aided by local guerrillas and resistance, he has however no way to take the city by force. He then started with his men in a campaign of sabotage and bombings that lasted more than a month. After having isolated the city by destroying the infrastructure surrounding it (overpasses, railway lines, bridges, etc.), the <a href="/wiki/French_Forces_of_the_Interior" title="French Forces of the Interior">FFI</a> had managed to rally the population and give the occupiers an impression of encirclement.</p>
<p>A mid-August 1944, Drouot-L'Hermine, who lost his right-hand man, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_H%C3%A9raud&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Paul Héraud (page does not exist)">Paul Héraud</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_H%C3%A9raud" title="fr:Paul Héraud">fr</a>)</span>, a few days earlier, sent two emissaries to negotiate the surrender of the Germans. The Germans were convinced of facing a large-scale uprising, and agreed to lay down their weapons provided that it was to regular troops (they refused, therefore, to surrender to the Resistance). While the Americans were more than 50 kilometres (31 mi) away, time was pressing for Drouot-L'Hermine. Indeed, he received an order from De Gaulle to liberate the city before the arrival of the Allies, to support the position of France as a victorious nation, liberated through the active participation of the Resistance. Drouot-L'Ermine then developed a new ploy. He managed to convince the Allies to advance one of their tanks into enemy terrain, and shoot a few rounds close to Gap. Shots echoed in the valley, and the Germans immediately identified the characteristic sound of a tank, a weapon that the guerrillas did not hold. Thinking they were then dealing with the Allies, the troops of the Reich surrendered to the Resistance. Therefore, a few hundred resistance fighters were able to capture 1,200 German soldiers, including 40 officers. The city was <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_II)#Liberation_of_France" title="Western Front (World War II)">liberated</a> on the evening of 19 August 1944.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fifth_Republic">Fifth Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Fifth Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The commune of <i>Romette</i> was associated with that of Gap, by decree dated 25 November 1974.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup></p>

</ul>
<p>Gap ran a bid to host the <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Olympics" title="2018 Winter Olympics">2018 Winter Olympics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> but lost out as France's candidate to nearby <a href="/wiki/Annecy" title="Annecy">Annecy</a>. The games were eventually awarded to <a href="/wiki/Pyeongchang_County" title="Pyeongchang County">Pyeongchang</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_administration">Politics and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Politics and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_trends_and_outcomes">Political trends and outcomes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Political trends and outcomes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: [[:<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=2014_municipal_elections_in_Haute-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="2014 municipal elections in Haute-Alpes (page does not exist)">2014 municipal elections in Haute-Alpes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89lections_municipales_de_2014_dans_les_Hautes-Alpes" title="fr:Élections municipales de 2014 dans les Hautes-Alpes">fr</a>)</span>]]</div>
<p>The outgoing mayor, Roger Didier, was a representative in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=2014_French_municipal_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="2014 French municipal elections (page does not exist)">municipal elections of 2014</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89lections_municipales_fran%C3%A7aises_de_2014" title="fr:Élections municipales françaises de 2014">fr</a>)</span> and was re-elected at the end of the second round with 53.37% of votes. The turnout was 57.41%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGfr5061_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-IGfr5061-58">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_administration">Municipal administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Municipal administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The City Council consists of 43 members, including 20 who are elected by the community council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGfr5061_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-IGfr5061-58">[57]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intercommunity">Intercommunity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Intercommunity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 1 January 2014, Gap is part of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Communaut%C3%A9_d%27agglom%C3%A9ration_du_Gapen%C3%A7ais&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Communauté d'agglomération du Gapençais (page does not exist)">Communauté d'agglomération du Gapençais</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communaut%C3%A9_d%27agglom%C3%A9ration_du_Gapen%C3%A7ais" title="fr:Communauté d'agglomération du Gapençais">fr</a>)</span> with the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/La_Freissinouse" title="La Freissinouse">La Freissinouse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pelleautier" title="Pelleautier">Pelleautier</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Until the departmental elections of March 2015, Gap was divided into six <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_the_Hautes-Alpes_department" title="Cantons of the Hautes-Alpes department">cantons</a>: <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Gap-Campagne" title="Canton of Gap-Campagne">Gap-Campagne</a> (including five communes: La Freissinouse, Manteyer, Pelleautier, Rabou and La Roche-des-Arnauds), <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Gap-Centre" title="Canton of Gap-Centre">Gap-Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Gap-Nord-Est" title="Canton of Gap-Nord-Est">Gap-Nord-Est</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Gap-Nord-Ouest" title="Canton of Gap-Nord-Ouest">Gap-Nord-Ouest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Gap-Sud-Est" title="Canton of Gap-Sud-Est">Gap-Sud-Est</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Gap-Sud-Ouest" title="Canton of Gap-Sud-Ouest">Gap-Sud-Ouest</a>.</p>
<p>Following the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=2014_redistricting_of_cantons_in_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="2014 redistricting of cantons in France (page does not exist)">redistribution of the cantons</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red%C3%A9coupage_cantonal_de_2014_en_France" title="fr:Redécoupage cantonal de 2014 en France">fr</a>)</span> of the Hautes-Alpes Department, Gap will include four cantons:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Canton_of_Gap-1&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Canton of Gap-1 (page does not exist)">Gap-1</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canton_de_Gap-1" title="fr:Canton de Gap-1">fr</a>)</span>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Canton_of_Gap-2&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Canton of Gap-2 (page does not exist)">Gap-2</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canton_de_Gap-2" title="fr:Canton de Gap-2">fr</a>)</span> (including <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Romette&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Romette (page does not exist)">Romette</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romette" title="fr:Romette">fr</a>)</span>), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Canton_of_Gap-3&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Canton of Gap-3 (page does not exist)">Gap-3</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canton_de_Gap-3" title="fr:Canton de Gap-3">fr</a>)</span> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Canton_of_Gap-4&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Canton of Gap-4 (page does not exist)">Gap-4</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canton_de_Gap-4" title="fr:Canton de Gap-4">fr</a>)</span>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_and_administrative_proceedings">Judicial and administrative proceedings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Judicial and administrative proceedings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gap has the presence of a high court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_policy">Environmental policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Environmental policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gap is classified as <i>three flowers</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Concours_des_villes_et_villages_fleuris" title="Concours des villes et villages fleuris">competition of flowery cities and villages</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="noviewer thumb tright">

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Twinning">Twinning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Twinning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Gap is twinned with a couple of European cities. It is in this framework that socio-cultural, educational and sports exchanges are made.</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy"><img alt="Italy" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/23px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/35px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/45px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Pinerolo" title="Pinerolo">Pinerolo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, since 1966<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VGjum_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-VGjum-66">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><img alt="Germany" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Traunstein" title="Traunstein">Traunstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, since 1976<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VGjum_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-VGjum-66">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Decentralised_cooperation">Decentralised cooperation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Decentralised cooperation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In addition, decentralised cooperation agreements have been signed with a couple of cities in Africa and Asia.</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon"><img alt="Cameroon" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Flag_of_Cameroon.svg/23px-Flag_of_Cameroon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Flag_of_Cameroon.svg/35px-Flag_of_Cameroon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Flag_of_Cameroon.svg/45px-Flag_of_Cameroon.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Bangou,_Cameroon" title="Bangou, Cameroon">Bangou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, since 2003<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal"><img alt="Nepal" data-file-height="885" data-file-width="726" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Flag_of_Nepal.svg/16px-Flag_of_Nepal.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Flag_of_Nepal.svg/25px-Flag_of_Nepal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Flag_of_Nepal.svg/33px-Flag_of_Nepal.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu" title="Kathmandu">Kathmandu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, since 2004<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_and_society">Population and society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Population and society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographic_change">Demographic change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Demographic change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2012, the commune had 40,761 inhabitants. The evolution of the number of inhabitants is known through the population censuses carried out in the town since 1793. From the 21st century, a census for communes with more than 10,000 inhabitants takes place every year as a result of a sample survey, unlike the other communes which have a real census every five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[note 3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[note 4]</a></sup></p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Age_structure">Age structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Age structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The population of the commune is relatively old. The proportion of people over 60 years of age (24.8%) is higher than the national proportion (21.6%) but is lower than the proportion in the Hautes-Alpes department as a whole (25%).</p>
<p>As in the national and departmental populations, the female population of the commune is greater than the male population. The rate (52.2%) is similar to the national rate (51.6%). In 2007, the distribution of the population of the commune, by age group, is as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>47.8% of males (0 to 14 years = 18%, 15–29 years = 18.7%, 30-44 year olds = 20.2%, 45–59 years = 21.1%, more than 60 years = 22%)</li>
<li>52.2% of females (0–14 years = 16.8%, 15–29 years = 16.2%, 30-44 year olds = 18.9%, 45–59 years = 20.9%, more than 60 years = 27.3%)</li>
</ul>
