<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gap is situated in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Acad%C3%A9mie_d%27Aix-Marseille&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Académie d'Aix-Marseille (page does not exist)">Académie d'Aix-Marseille</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Acad%C3%A9mie_d%27Aix-Marseille" title="fr:Académie d'Aix-Marseille">fr</a>)</span>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The city administers 12 <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89cole_maternelle_in_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="École maternelle in France (page does not exist)">nursery schools</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89cole_maternelle_en_France" title="fr:École maternelle en France">fr</a>)</span>, 13 <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89cole_%C3%A9l%C3%A9mentaire_in_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="École élémentaire in France (page does not exist)">elementary schools</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89cole_%C3%A9l%C3%A9mentaire_en_France" title="fr:École élémentaire en France">fr</a>)</span> and 6 rural schools. There are also several private kindergartens and elementary schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Department manages five <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Coll%C3%A8ge_in_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Collège in France (page does not exist)">collèges</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coll%C3%A8ge_en_France" title="fr:Collège en France">fr</a>)</span> and four <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education_in_France" title="Secondary education in France">lycées</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" title="Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur">Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur</a> region, the Lycée professionnel Paul-Hariharan, the school of general and farm technology education "Les Emeyères", the Dominique-Villars Lycée and the Aristide-Briand Lycée.</p>
<p>There are also two private schools, the Lycée professionnel Sévigné and Lycée Saint-Joseph. That said, the Lycée professionnel Sévigné is now public.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VilleGap050.jpg"><img alt="Université d'Aix-Marseille, pôle university in Gap." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/VilleGap050.jpg/220px-VilleGap050.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/VilleGap050.jpg/330px-VilleGap050.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/VilleGap050.jpg/440px-VilleGap050.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VilleGap050.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pôle University in Gap</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Higher education in Gap is represented by the Pôle University of Gap, an annex of the former <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Mediterranean" title="University of the Mediterranean">University of the Mediterranean Aix-Marseille II</a>, today the <a href="/wiki/Aix-Marseille_University" title="Aix-Marseille University">Aix-Marseille University</a>, created from the merger of three universities. It includes a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sciences_et_techniques_des_activit%C3%A9s_physiques_et_sportives&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sciences et techniques des activités physiques et sportives (page does not exist)">STAPS</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sciences_et_techniques_des_activit%C3%A9s_physiques_et_sportives" title="fr:Sciences et techniques des activités physiques et sportives">fr</a>)</span> centre, a Business Administration and Management <a href="/wiki/University_Institutes_of_Technology" title="University Institutes of Technology">IUT</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GEA_France" title="GEA France">GEA</a>), a "Mountain crafts" <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Institut_universitaire_professionnalis%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Institut universitaire professionnalisé (page does not exist)">IUP</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institut_universitaire_professionnalis%C3%A9" title="fr:Institut universitaire professionnalisé">fr</a>)</span> (professional master) which is unique in France, as well as being able to give an aircraft maintenance licence (<a href="/wiki/Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" title="Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur">Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur</a> region is a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=P%C3%B4le_de_comp%C3%A9titivit%C3%A9_in_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pôle de compétitivité in France (page does not exist)">Competitive Centre</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/P%C3%B4le_de_comp%C3%A9titivit%C3%A9_en_France" title="fr:Pôle de compétitivité en France">fr</a>)</span> in <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics" title="Aeronautics">Aeronautics</a>, and the Department has established the Centre of Rural Excellence <i>Excell'Air</i>.</p>
<p>Several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brevet_de_Technicien_Sup%C3%A9rieur" title="Brevet de Technicien Supérieur">BTS</a> chains and preparatory classes exist in the lycées, in particular a Computer Services in Organisations BTS and a Negotiations and Customer Service BTS at the Lycée Dominique Villars as well as an Assistant Manager BTS at the Lycée Aristide Briand.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_events_and_festivities">Cultural events and festivities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Cultural events and festivities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the summer months, the association of merchants of the town centre <i>Les Vitrines de Gap</i> organises Nocturnes. These are musical and festive events accompanied by the opening of stores downtown from 7pm until 11pm. Each year an Expo Fair also takes place at the Parc de la Pépinnière during May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Quattro, a theatre with retractable tiered seating, organises all kinds of events, namely concerts, performances, business seminars, etc.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city has a hospital, the Centre Hospitalier Intercommunal of Alpes du Sud (CHICAS) which is divided into three entities. The first and most important site is Gap, which is the largest hospital of the Southern Alps. Gap is also equipped with a site specialising in geriatrics. As a result of a merger, the CHICAS manages the site of <a href="/wiki/Sisteron" title="Sisteron">Sisteron</a>. The Polyclinic of the Southern Alps is the only clinic present in the city and other centres of rehabilitation.</p>
<p>There is also a Maison Médicale du Gapençais with extended opening hours.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gap-Janv2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Gap-Janv2013.jpg/220px-Gap-Janv2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Gap-Janv2013.jpg/330px-Gap-Janv2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Gap-Janv2013.jpg/440px-Gap-Janv2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<p>Clubs:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">Ice hockey</a> club, the <a href="/wiki/Rapaces_de_Gap" title="Rapaces de Gap">Rapaces de Gap</a> [Gap Raptors], which plays in <a href="/wiki/Ligue_Magnus" title="Ligue Magnus">Ligue Magnus</a> and has more than 30 titles of champion of France in all categories.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Gap_FC" title="Gap FC">Gap FC</a> football team, which plays in the 1st division of the Alps District.</li>
<li>The athletic club, the Gap Hautes-Alpes athletics (GH2A).</li>
<li>Cross-country ski club, Ski club Gap-Bayard.</li>
<li>Road cycling and mountain biking club, the UCPG.</li>
<li>Mountain biking club, the PJPC.</li>
<li><i>Gap Hautes Alpes Rugby</i> club plays in <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9rale_3" title="Fédérale 3">Fédérale 3</a>.</li>
<li>Gap basketball for <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Championnat_Pr%C3%A9-nationale_R%C3%A9gionale_de_basket-ball&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Championnat Pré-nationale Régionale de basket-ball (page does not exist)">Pre-nationale</a>.</li>
<li>Gap Handball playing in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Championnat_Pr%C3%A9nationale_R%C3%A9gionale_de_handball&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Championnat Prénationale Régionale de handball (page does not exist)">Pre-nationale</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Championnat_Pr%C3%A9nationale_R%C3%A9gionale_de_handball" title="fr:Championnat Prénationale Régionale de handball">fr</a>)</span>.</li>
<li>Gap volleyball which plays in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Championnat_R%C3%A9gional&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Championnat Régional (page does not exist)">Regional Championship</a>.</li>
<li>The Gapencais Sasquatches, club allowing the discovery or the practice of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Football" title="American Football">American Football</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>The town of Gap regularly hosts stages of the <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Crit%C3%A9rium_du_Dauphin%C3%A9" title="Critérium du Dauphiné">Critérium du Dauphiné</a> in cycling, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Monte_Carlo_Rally" title="Monte Carlo Rally">Monte Carlo Rally</a> in motorsport.</p>
<p>The town of Gap is known for its mountain bike trek the <i>Paths of the Sun</i>, between <a href="/wiki/Saillans,_Dr%C3%B4me" title="Saillans, Drôme">Saillans</a> and Gap.</p>
<p>The sports facilities in Gap include stadiums, gymnasiums, swimming pools, <a href="/wiki/Patinoire_Brown-Ferrand" title="Patinoire Brown-Ferrand">ice rink</a>, multi-purpose room (bowling), and tennis courts.</p>
<p>The fitness centre Gap-Bayard, located on the Bayard plateau, has a 18-hole golf course that operates in summer and is a base for <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing" title="Cross-country skiing">cross-country skiing</a> in winter.</p>
<p>In October 2004, the association <i>Objective JO 2018</i> worked for a French candidacy of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alpes_du_Sud_(France)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alpes du Sud (France) (page does not exist)">Alpes du Sud</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpes_du_Sud_(France)" title="fr:Alpes du Sud (France)">fr</a>)</span>, at the <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Olympics" title="2018 Winter Olympics">2018 Winter Olympics</a>. The town of Gap was approached to run in the race. Gap withdrew in October 2008 and was replaced by the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Pelvoux" title="Pelvoux">Pelvoux</a> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Communaut%C3%A9_de_communes_du_Pays_des_%C3%89crins&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Communauté de communes du Pays des Écrins (page does not exist)">Communauté de communes du Pays des Écrins</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communaut%C3%A9_de_communes_du_Pays_des_%C3%89crins" title="fr:Communauté de communes du Pays des Écrins">fr</a>)</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, the town of Gap won the competition of the <i><a href="/wiki/Intervilles" title="Intervilles">Intervilles</a></i> sports show during the final against Dax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>The town of Gap hosted the final of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Coupe_de_France_des_rallyes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Coupe de France des rallyes (page does not exist)">Coupe de France des rallyes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coupe_de_France_des_rallyes" title="fr:Coupe de France des rallyes">fr</a>)</span> amateurs during the autumn of 2012.</p>
<p>In 2013, the town of Gap was elected the sportiest city of more of 20,000 inhabitants in France by <i><a href="/wiki/L%27%C3%89quipe" title="L'Équipe">L'Équipe</a></i> newspaper.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Catholic">Catholic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Catholic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Gap" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Gap">Roman Catholic Diocese of Gap</a></div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Cathedral_and_churches">Cathedral and churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Cathedral and churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Gap_Cathedral" title="Gap Cathedral">Cathedral of Notre-Dame and Saint-Arnoux</a>, built in the 19th century according to the plans of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_Laisn%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Charles Laisné (page does not exist)">Charles Laisné</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Laisn%C3%A9" title="fr:Charles Laisné">fr</a>)</span>.</li>
<li>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89glise_Saint-Andr%C3%A9-les-Cordeliers_de_Gap&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Église Saint-André-les-Cordeliers de Gap (page does not exist)">Church of Saint-André-les-Cordeliers</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89glise_Saint-Andr%C3%A9-les-Cordeliers_de_Gap" title="fr:Église Saint-André-les-Cordeliers de Gap">fr</a>)</span>, rebuilt in the 18th century and used to worship according to the <a href="/wiki/Tridentine_Mass" title="Tridentine Mass">extraordinary rite</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>.</li>
<li>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89glise_Saint-Roch_de_Gap&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Église Saint-Roch de Gap (page does not exist)">Church of Saint-Roch</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89glise_Saint-Roch_de_Gap" title="fr:Église Saint-Roch de Gap">fr</a>)</span>, built in the 20th century.</li>
<li>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89glise_Notre-Dame-d%27Esp%C3%A9rance_de_Gap&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Église Notre-Dame-d'Espérance de Gap (page does not exist)">Church our Lady of Hope</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89glise_Notre-Dame-d%27Esp%C3%A9rance_de_Gap" title="fr:Église Notre-Dame-d'Espérance de Gap">fr</a>)</span>, built in the 20th century.</li>
<li>St. Peter's Church</li>
</ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Muslim">Muslim</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Muslim">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>The Al Salam Mosque, inaugurated on 7 July 2013<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revenues_of_the_population_and_taxation">Revenues of the population and taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Revenues of the population and taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Revenues">Revenues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Revenues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The median pay in Gap in 2011 is 18,944 euros. The majority of revenues are derived from wage work (55%), compared to a third of retirees (30%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insee05061_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-insee05061-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">Taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2011, 18,345 households existed in Gap, 60% of them were taxable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insee05061_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-insee05061-23">[23]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=B%C3%A2timent_et_travaux_publics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bâtiment et travaux publics (page does not exist)">BTP sector</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%A2timent_et_travaux_publics" title="fr:Bâtiment et travaux publics">fr</a>)</span> has grown through the inclusion of winter sports.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary_sector">Tertiary sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Tertiary sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The tertiary sector is the sector which dominates the local economy:</p>
<ul>
<li>Garrison town (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=4th_Mountain_Infantry_Battalion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="4th Mountain Infantry Battalion (page does not exist)">4th Mountain Infantry Battalion</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/4e_r%C3%A9giment_de_chasseurs" title="fr:4e régiment de chasseurs">fr</a>)</span> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Base_de_D%C3%A9fense&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Base de Défense (page does not exist)">Base de Défense</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Base_de_D%C3%A9fense" title="fr:Base de Défense">fr</a>)</span> since January 2011)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[83]</a></sup> and administrative (prefecture, department hall)</li>
<li>Tourism</li>
</ul>
<p>Gap is the seat of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chambre_de_commerce_et_d%27industrie_des_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chambre de commerce et d'industrie des Hautes-Alpes (page does not exist)">Chamber of commerce and industry of the Hautes-Alpes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chambre_de_commerce_et_d%27industrie_des_Hautes-Alpes" title="fr:Chambre de commerce et d'industrie des Hautes-Alpes">fr</a>)</span>. It manages the Centre for regional and European tourism (CRET) of <a href="/wiki/Brian%C3%A7on" title="Briançon">Briançon</a>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=ADAPEI&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="ADAPEI (page does not exist)">ADAPEI</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adapei" title="fr:Adapei">fr</a>)</span> of Gap and the <i>Centre Européen Médical Bioclimatique de Recherche et d'Enseignement Universitaire</i> [European medical bioclimatic research and university teaching Center] (CEMBREU) of Briançon.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_culture_and_heritage">Local culture and heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Local culture and heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_and_monuments">Places and monuments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Places and monuments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mus%C3%A9e_Mus%C3%A9um_d%C3%A9partemental_des_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Musée Muséum départemental des Hautes-Alpes (page does not exist)">Departemental Museum of the Hautes-Alpes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_Mus%C3%A9um_d%C3%A9partemental_des_Hautes-Alpes" title="fr:Musée Muséum départemental des Hautes-Alpes">fr</a>)</span> houses the mausoleum of <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Bonne,_Duke_of_Lesdigui%C3%A8res" title="François de Bonne, Duke of Lesdiguières">François de Bonne</a> (Duke of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Duchy_of_Lesdigui%C3%A8res&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Duchy of Lesdiguières (page does not exist)">Lesdiguières</a>, Constable of the Haut-Alpin) carved in the black marble of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Champsaur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Champsaur (page does not exist)">Champsaur</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Champsaur" title="fr:Champsaur">fr</a>)</span> by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jacob_Richier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jacob Richier (page does not exist)">Jacob Richier</a>.</li>
<li>The pedestrian centre made of small passages and pleasant terraces revolves around place Jean-Marcellin.</li>
<li>Bronze by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cyril_de_La_Patelli%C3%A8re&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cyril de La Patellière (page does not exist)">Cyril de La Patellière</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyril_de_La_Patelli%C3%A8re" title="fr:Cyril de La Patellière">fr</a>)</span>, "The Light", by order of Mayor <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Bernard-Reymond" title="Pierre Bernard-Reymond">Pierre Bernard-Reymond</a> in 2006.</li>
<li>The Parc de la Pépinière</li>
<li>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=La_Tour_de_l%27Horloge_de_Gap&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="La Tour de l'Horloge de Gap (page does not exist)">clock tower</a></li>
<li>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=L%27H%C3%B4tel-de-Ville_de_Gap&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="L'Hôtel-de-Ville de Gap (page does not exist)">town hall</a></li>
<li>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89glise_Saint-Andr%C3%A9-les-Cordeliers_de_Gap&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Église Saint-André-les-Cordeliers de Gap (page does not exist)">*Church of Saint André les Cordeliers</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89glise_Saint-Andr%C3%A9-les-Cordeliers_de_Gap" title="fr:Église Saint-André-les-Cordeliers de Gap">fr</a>)</span></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Gap_Cathedral" title="Gap Cathedral">Cathedral of Notre-Dame and Saint-Arnoux</a> was built from 1866 to 1904 according to the plans of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_Laisn%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Charles Laisné (page does not exist)">Charles Laisné</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Laisn%C3%A9" title="fr:Charles Laisné">fr</a>)</span>. This <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Neo-Gothic</a> building replaces a medieval construction.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Conservatoire_botanique_national_alpin_de_Gap-Charance" title="Conservatoire botanique national alpin de Gap-Charance">Conservatoire botanique national alpin de Gap-Charance</a>, situated north-west of Gap</li>
</ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Charance_Estate">The Charance Estate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: The Charance Estate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gap014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1500" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gap014.jpg/220px-Gap014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gap014.jpg/330px-Gap014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gap014.jpg/440px-Gap014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gap014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Charance Lake</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panoramique_gap_ggielly.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="630" data-file-width="1450" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Panoramique_gap_ggielly.jpg/220px-Panoramique_gap_ggielly.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Panoramique_gap_ggielly.jpg/330px-Panoramique_gap_ggielly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Panoramique_gap_ggielly.jpg/440px-Panoramique_gap_ggielly.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Panoramique_gap_ggielly.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The city of Gap seen from Charance</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Château de Charance was built in the 16th century. It includes a main building, which today is the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/%C3%89crins_National_Park" title="Écrins National Park">Écrins National Park</a>, and several annexes, one of which houses the Park Museum.</p>
<p>The Charance Estate also features the Conservatoire botanique national alpin [Alpine National Botanical Conservatory], a terraced garden and an area of 220 hectares (540 acres) around the <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau" title="Château">château</a> and in the middle of which lies a small lake: Charance Lake. All overlooks the city.</p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: [[:<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Domaine_de_Charance&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Domaine de Charance (page does not exist)">Domaine de Charance</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domaine_de_Charance" title="fr:Domaine de Charance">fr</a>)</span>]]</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_heritage">Cultural heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Cultural heritage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The theatre of La Passerelle, <i>Scène nationale</i> [national stage] of the Southern Alps.</li>
<li>The Quattro, a versatile new cultural space initially called the "Cube", inaugurated on 27 May 2008</li>
<li>The Conservatoire, of departmental influence</li>
<li>The Municipal Centre of Culture and Leisure (CMCL)</li>
<li>The municipal library</li>
<li>The international Folkdance festival, which takes place every year in July</li>
<li>3 cinemas exist in Gap (of which two have been saved by the city hall, when the building housing their screens was sold)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[84]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_life">Military life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Military life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Military units have been stationed at Gap:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/17th_Infantry_Regiment_(France)" title="17th Infantry Regiment (France)">17th infantry regiment</a>, before 1914</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/96th_Infantry_Regiment_(France)" title="96th Infantry Regiment (France)">96th infantry regiment</a>, 1906</li>
<li>7th Demi-brigade of Mountain Infantry, 1939-1940, consisting of:
<ul>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=6th_Mountain_Infantry_Battalion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="6th Mountain Infantry Battalion (page does not exist)">6th Mountain Infantry Battalion</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/6e_bataillon_de_chasseurs_alpins" title="fr:6e bataillon de chasseurs alpins">fr</a>)</span></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=15th_Mountain_Infantry_Battalion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="15th Mountain Infantry Battalion (page does not exist)">15th Mountain Infantry Battalion</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/15e_bataillon_de_chasseurs_alpins" title="fr:15e bataillon de chasseurs alpins">fr</a>)</span></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=23rd_Mountain_Infantry_Battalion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="23rd Mountain Infantry Battalion (page does not exist)">23rd Mountain Infantry Battalion</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/23e_bataillon_de_chasseurs_alpins" title="fr:23e bataillon de chasseurs alpins">fr</a>)</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>4th Mountain Infantry Battalion (4th Rch) since 1983.</p>

Statue of Ladoucette in Gap made by the Gap sculptor, Jean Marcellin</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Below is a non-exhaustive list of people born in Gap or having a particular attachment to the city:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9raud_de_Nice" title="Féraud de Nice">Féraud de Nice</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 970</span> - 1044) - Bishop of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Gap" title="Bishopric of Gap">Gap</a> at the beginning of the 11th century.</li>
<li>Albertet of Sisteron (1194-1221) - native <a href="/wiki/Troubadour" title="Troubadour">troubadour</a> of the town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[85]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_Farel" title="William Farel">Guillaume Farel</a> (1489-1565) - Protestant reformer, he participated in the expansion of the Protestant Reformation in French-speaking Switzerland and was a translator of the Bible to French and Occitan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[86]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Honorat_Rambaud&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Honorat Rambaud (page does not exist)">Honorat Rambaud</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honorat_Rambaud" title="fr:Honorat Rambaud">fr</a>)</span> (1516-1586) - Marseille grammarian, born in Gap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[87]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Honor%C3%A9_Pell%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Honoré Pellé (page does not exist)">Honoré Pellé</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honor%C3%A9_Pell%C3%A9" title="fr:Honoré Pellé">fr</a>)</span> or Honoré Pela (1641-1718) - baroque sculptor, pupil of <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Puget" title="Pierre Puget">Pierre Puget</a>, his career took place mainly in <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jean-Michel_Rolland&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jean-Michel Rolland (page does not exist)">Jean-Michel Rolland</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Michel_Rolland" title="fr:Jean-Michel Rolland">fr</a>)</span> (1745-1810) - parish priest of <a href="/wiki/Le_Caire" title="Le Caire">Le Caire</a> in 1789, Deputy to the <a href="/wiki/Estates-General_of_1789" title="Estates-General of 1789">Estates-General of 1789</a> and the constituent Assembly (1789-1791).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[89]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dominique_Villars" title="Dominique Villars">Dominique Villars</a> (1745-1814) - botanist, he is the author of several manuscripts of <i>Histoire des plantes du Dauphiné</i> resulting from over twenty years of observations of plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[90]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jean_Labastie&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jean Labastie (page does not exist)">Jean Labastie</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Labastie" title="fr:Jean Labastie">fr</a>)</span> (1754-1821) - born in Gap, former National Assembly member for Hautes-Alpes</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Joseph_Provensal_de_Lompr%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Joseph Provensal de Lompré (page does not exist)">Joseph Provensal de Lompré</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Provensal_de_Lompr%C3%A9" title="fr:Joseph Provensal de Lompré">fr</a>)</span> (1760-1833) – died in Gap, former National Assembly member for Hautes-Alpes and imperial attorney</li>
<li>Baron <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Charles-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Ladoucette&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Charles-François de Ladoucette (page does not exist)">Charles-François de Ladoucette</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Ladoucette" title="fr:Charles-François de Ladoucette">fr</a>)</span> (1772-1848) - prefect of Hautes-Alpes under <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>. He founded the <i>Société d'émulation des Hautes-Alpes</i> [Society of Emulation of Haute-Alpes] (now the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_d%27%C3%A9tudes_des_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Société d'études des Hautes-Alpes (page does not exist)">Society for the Study of the Hautes-Alpes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_d%27%C3%A9tudes_des_Hautes-Alpes" title="fr:Société d'études des Hautes-Alpes">fr</a>)</span>) and Gap Museum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Honor%C3%A9_Bucelle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Honoré Bucelle (page does not exist)">Honoré Bucelle</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honor%C3%A9_Bucelle" title="fr:Honoré Bucelle">fr</a>)</span> (1762-1844), died in Gap, from 1820 to 1827 National Assembly member for <a href="/wiki/Hautes-Alpes" title="Hautes-Alpes">Hautes-Alpes</a> .</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph-Bruno_Guigues" title="Joseph-Bruno Guigues">Joseph-Bruno Guigues</a> (1805-1874) - first bishop of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bishopric_of_Ottawa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bishopric of Ottawa (page does not exist)">Ottawa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[92]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Colomb_de_Batines" title="Paul Colomb de Batines">Paul Colomb de Batines</a> (1811–1855), Librarian and bibliographer</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jean_Marcellin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jean Marcellin (page does not exist)">Jean Marcellin</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Marcellin" title="fr:Jean Marcellin">fr</a>)</span> (1821-1884) - sculptor, pupil of <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Rude" title="François Rude">François Rude</a>. Gap owes him for the Baron of Ladoucette statue at the end of the course Ladoucette.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jules-Henri-Marius_Bergeret&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jules-Henri-Marius Bergeret (page does not exist)">Jules-Henri-Marius Bergeret</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jules-Henri-Marius_Bergeret" title="fr:Jules-Henri-Marius Bergeret">fr</a>)</span> was born in Gap (Hautes-Alpes) in 1830 and died in New York (United States) in 1905, was a personality of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Commune" title="Paris Commune">Paris Commune</a>.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Auguste_Burle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Auguste Burle (page does not exist)">Auguste Burle</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auguste_et_%C3%89mile_Burle" title="fr:Auguste et Émile Burle">fr</a>)</span> (1834-1889) and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Emile_Burle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Emile Burle (page does not exist)">Emile Burle</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auguste_et_%C3%89mile_Burle" title="fr:Auguste et Émile Burle">fr</a>)</span> (1835-1875) were botanists, specialists of the flora in the vicinity of Gap, they donated their Herbarium at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_linn%C3%A9enne_de_Lyon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Société linnéenne de Lyon (page does not exist)">Botanical Society of Lyon</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_linn%C3%A9enne_de_Lyon" title="fr:Société linnéenne de Lyon">fr</a>)</span>.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Joseph_Roman&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Joseph Roman (page does not exist)">Joseph Roman</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Roman" title="fr:Joseph Roman">fr</a>)</span> (1850-1924) - Director of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Archives_d%C3%A9partementales_des_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Archives départementales des Hautes-Alpes (page does not exist)">Archives of Hautes-Alpes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archives_d%C3%A9partementales_des_Hautes-Alpes" title="fr:Archives départementales des Hautes-Alpes">fr</a>)</span>, and as historian, he published several brochures on cities, villages and the families of his departement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[94]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hippolyte_M%C3%BCller&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hippolyte Müller (page does not exist)">Hippolyte Müller</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hippolyte_M%C3%BCller" title="fr:Hippolyte Müller">fr</a>)</span> (1865-1933) - originally an apprentice jeweller, a self-taught archaeologist, he was the founder of the <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_dauphinois" title="Musée dauphinois">Musée dauphinois</a> at Grenoble.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[95]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Georges_de_Manteyer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Georges de Manteyer (page does not exist)">Georges de Manteyer</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georges_de_Manteyer" title="fr:Georges de Manteyer">fr</a>)</span> (1867-1948) - historian, Chief Archivist of the Hautes-Alpes, his bust was erected in the Parc de la Pépinière, in the centre of Gap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Louise_Germain" title="Louise Germain">Louise Germain</a> (1874-1939) - painter who often worked alongside <a href="/wiki/Paul_C%C3%A9zanne" title="Paul Cézanne">Paul Cézanne</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Achille_Mauzan" title="Achille Mauzan">Achille Mauzan</a> (1883-1952) - artist from <a href="/wiki/Gaumont_Film_Company" title="Gaumont Film Company">Gaumont</a> cinema at the beginning of the 20th century. He was also a painter and sculptor and was part of the <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> art movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[97]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Andr%C3%A9_Allix&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="André Allix (page does not exist)">André Allix</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Allix" title="fr:André Allix">fr</a>)</span> (1889-1966) - geographer, former Rector of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Lyon" title="University of Lyon">University of Lyon</a> and former Director of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=G%C3%A9ocarrefour&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Géocarrefour (page does not exist)"><i>Revue de Géographie de Lyon</i></a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%A9ocarrefour" title="fr:Géocarrefour">fr</a>)</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[98]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jean_Michard-Pellissier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jean Michard-Pellissier (page does not exist)">Jean Michard-Pellissier</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Michard-Pellissier" title="fr:Jean Michard-Pellissier">fr</a>)</span> (1909-1976) - born in Gap, politician.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Thomas_(director)" title="Robert Thomas (director)">Robert Thomas</a> (1927-1989) - born in Gap, playwright, director and producer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[100]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jacques_Bolognesi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jacques Bolognesi (page does not exist)">Jacques Bolognesi</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacques_Bolognesi" title="fr:Jacques Bolognesi">fr</a>)</span> (1947-) - born in Gap, composer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[101]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Henri_Br%C3%A9chu" title="Henri Bréchu">Henri Bréchu</a> (1947-) - born in Gap, skier.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Francis_Masse" title="Francis Masse">Francis Masse</a> (1948-) - born in Gap, screenwriter and comic illustrator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[102]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marie-Anne_Chazel" title="Marie-Anne Chazel">Marie-Anne Chazel</a> (1951-) - born in Gap, actress, Member of <a href="/wiki/Le_Splendid" title="Le Splendid">Le Splendid</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Raymond_Durand_(driver)" title="Raymond Durand (driver)">Raymond Durand</a> (1952-) - born in Gap, rally driver, champion of the world <a href="/wiki/FIA_Alternative_Energies_Cup" title="FIA Alternative Energies Cup">FIA Alternative Energies Cup</a> in 2009 and 2010.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chantal_Lauby" title="Chantal Lauby">Chantal Lauby</a> (1953-) - born in Gap, comedian, film director, actress, Member of <a href="/wiki/Les_Nuls" title="Les Nuls">Les Nuls</a>.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Michel_Crespin_(author)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Michel Crespin (author) (page does not exist)">Michel Crespin</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michel_Crespin_(auteur)" title="fr:Michel Crespin (auteur)">fr</a>)</span> (1955-2001) - born in Gap, French cartoonist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[103]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christian_Audigier" title="Christian Audigier">Christian Audigier</a> (1958-), designer</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pierre_Granoux&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pierre Granoux (page does not exist)">Pierre Granoux</a> (1963-) - artist, organizer of exhibitions and art publisher. Currently lives in Berlin, Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[104]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jean-Christophe_Lafaille" title="Jean-Christophe Lafaille">Jean-Christophe Lafaille</a> (1965-2006)-born in Gap, mountaineer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fabienne_Berthaud" title="Fabienne Berthaud">Fabienne Berthaud</a> (1966–), writer, actress and director, was born in Gap</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christian_Pouget" title="Christian Pouget">Christian Pouget</a> (1966-) - born in Gap, hockey player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[106]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gilles_Grimandi" title="Gilles Grimandi">Gilles Grimandi</a> (1970-) - born in Gap, footballer.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=R%C3%A9becca_Dautremer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rébecca Dautremer (page does not exist)">Rébecca Dautremer</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%C3%A9becca_Dautremer" title="fr:Rébecca Dautremer">fr</a>)</span> (1971-) - born in Gap, graphic designer, illustrator and author of children's books.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Laurence_Manfredi" title="Laurence Manfredi">Laurence Manfredi</a> (1974-) - born in Gap, athlete.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Julien_Blanc-Gras&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Julien Blanc-Gras (page does not exist)">Julien Blanc-Gras</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julien_Blanc-Gras" title="fr:Julien Blanc-Gras">fr</a>)</span> (1976-) - born in Gap, journalist and writer.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Camille_Combal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Camille Combal (page does not exist)">Camille Combal</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camille_Combal" title="fr:Camille Combal">fr</a>)</span> (1981-) - born in Gap, comedian, radio and television host.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9bastien_Ogier" title="Sébastien Ogier">Sébastien Ogier</a> (1983-) - born in Gap, rally driver, 3 time World Rally Champion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[107]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/La%C3%ABtitia_Roux" title="Laëtitia Roux">Laëtitia Roux</a> (1985-) - born in Gap, specialist ski mountaineer and trail.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St%C3%A9phane_Tempier" title="Stéphane Tempier">Stéphane Tempier</a> (1986-) - born in Gap, competed in the 2012 Olympics in mountain biking.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heraldry">Heraldry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Heraldry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center;padding:5px 8px;width:120px;">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blason_Gap.svg" title="Arms of Gap"><img alt="Arms of Gap" data-file-height="660" data-file-width="600" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Blason_Gap.svg/120px-Blason_Gap.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Blason_Gap.svg/180px-Blason_Gap.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Blason_Gap.svg/240px-Blason_Gap.svg.png 2x" width="120"/></a></div>
</div>
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top;">The arms of Gap are <a href="/wiki/Blazon" title="Blazon">blazoned</a> :<br/>
<i><a href="/wiki/Azure_(heraldry)" title="Azure (heraldry)">Azure</a>, a castle of <a href="/wiki/Or_(heraldry)" title="Or (heraldry)">or</a> with <a href="/wiki/Sable_(heraldry)" title="Sable (heraldry)">sable</a> crenellated masonry, with an amount of four towers of the same, covered point.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[108]</a></sup>
<p><br/></p>
<p><br/></p>
</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gap,_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-count references-column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">However, these terms have not been of Germanic influence in the other Romance languages, including <a href="/wiki/Proven%C3%A7al_dialect" title="Provençal dialect">Provençal</a> : Latin <i>vespa</i> &gt; Provençal <i>vespa</i>, Latin <i>viscum</i> &gt; Provençal <i>vesc</i>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-61"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-61">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Former 1st Deputy and member of the left-wing majority to the general <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Conseil_d%C3%A9partemental_des_Hautes-Alpes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Conseil départemental des Hautes-Alpes (page does not exist)">Council of the Hautes-Alpes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conseil_d%C3%A9partemental_des_Hautes-Alpes" title="fr:Conseil départemental des Hautes-Alpes">fr</a>)</span>, Roger Didier was elected Mayor following the resignation of Pierre Bernard-Reymond (UMP) who became Senator on 26 January 2007. Due to the Act on the <a href="/wiki/Dual_mandate" title="Dual mandate">accumulation of mandates</a>, he preferred to keep his mandate to advise the <a href="/wiki/Regional_council_(France)" title="Regional council (France)">regional council</a> of <a href="/wiki/Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" title="Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur">Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur</a>.<br/>
Source: <cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20081123102321/http://www.bulletindescommunes.fr/eu/index.php?news=683" rel="nofollow">"Sarkozy aux Allemands: "vous êtes un modèle, on va faire tout comme vous!<span style="padding-right:0.2em;">"</span>" [Sarkozy to the Germans: "You are a model, we'll do just like you!"]</a> (in French). Archived from <a class="external text" href="http://www.bulletindescommunes.fr/eu/index.php?news=683" rel="nofollow">the original</a> on 23 November 2008<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">11 April</span> 2015</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGap%2C+Hautes-Alpes&amp;rft.btitle=Sarkozy+aux+Allemands%3A+%22vous+%C3%AAtes+un+mod%C3%A8le%2C+on+va+faire+tout+comme+vous%21%22&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.bulletindescommunes.fr%2Feu%2Findex.php%3Fnews%3D683&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-71"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-71">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">At the beginning of the 21st century, the terms of census have been amended by <a class="external text" href="http://www.legifrance.gouv.fr/affichTexte.do?cidTexte=JORFTEXT000000593100&amp;fastPos=1&amp;fastReqId=2036940488&amp;categorieLien=cid&amp;oldAction=rechTexte" rel="nofollow">Act No. 2002-276 of 27 February 2002</a>, known as the 'law of democracy of proximity' relating to local democracy, and in particular title V "census operations", in order to allow, after a transitional period running from 2004 to 2008, the annual publication of the legal population of the different French administrative districts. For communes with a population of over 10,000 inhabitants, a sample survey is carried out each year, all of the territory of these communes is taken into account at the end of the same period of five years. The first legal population later than 1999 and within this new system came into force on 1 January 1, 2009 and corresponds to the Census of 2006.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-72">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the table of censuses, by convention in Wikipedia, the principle has been retained for legal populations after 1999 to display in the table of censuses that populations corresponding to the year 2006, first published legal population calculated in accordance with the concepts defined in Decree No. 2003-485 of 5 June 2003, and the years corresponding to an exhaustive census investigation of communes under 10,000 inhabitants, and in the years 2006, 2011, 2016, etc. for the communes with more than 10,000 inhabitants, as well as the last legal population published by Insee for the Communes as a whole.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
